# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4`

# Task: Implement Bulk Silence Creation API for Prometheus

## Objective
Add a new `/api/v1/silences/bulk` POST endpoint to Prometheus that accepts an array of
silence definitions and creates them atomically.

## Requirements

1. **Create handler in `web/api/v1/api.go`** (or a new file `web/api/v1/silences_bulk.go`):
   - Register new route `/api/v1/silences/bulk` in the API router
   - Accept JSON array of silence objects (same schema as single silence)
   - Validate all silences before creating any (atomic semantics)
   - Return array of created silence IDs on success
   - Return detailed error with index of failing silence on validation failure

2. **Follow existing patterns**:
   - Study how `/api/v1/silences` POST handler works for single silence creation
   - Use the same alertmanager client interface for silence management
   - Follow the same error response format (apiError struct)

3. **Create test file** `web/api/v1/silences_bulk_test.go`:
   - Test successful bulk creation
   - Test validation failure (bad matchers)
   - Test empty array handling
   - Test partial validation failure

## Key Reference Files
- `web/api/v1/api.go` — API router registration and handler patterns
- `web/api/v1/api_test.go` — test patterns for API endpoints
- `silence/silence.go` — silence model and validation

## Success Criteria
- Bulk endpoint handler function exists
- Route registered in API router
- Accepts array input and returns array of IDs
- Has proper error handling following Prometheus patterns
- Test file with test functions exists

## Summary of Prometheus Repository Analysis

Based on my thorough search of the Prometheus repository at `github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4`, here's what I found regarding silence-related code, API patterns, and existing implementations:

### Key Findings:

#### 1. **Silence Handling in Prometheus**
- Prometheus itself does NOT implement silence management. Silence handling is a feature of **Alertmanager**, not Prometheus.
- References to silences are mentioned in documentation (`docs/configuration/alerting_rules.md`) which states: "Another layer is needed to add summarization, notification rate limiting, **silencing** and alert dependencies on top of the simple alert definitions. In Prometheus's ecosystem, the [Alertmanager](https://prometheus.io/docs/alerting/alertmanager/) takes on this role."

#### 2. **API Structure and Patterns** (from `/web/api/v1/api.go`)
The Prometheus API follows these patterns:

**Endpoint Registration (lines 372-459):**
```go
func (api *API) Register(r *route.Router) {
    // Pattern: r.Get/Post/Del("/endpoint_path", wrap(api.handlerFunction))
    r.Get("/query", wrapAgent(api.query))
    r.Post("/query", wrapAgent(api.query))
    r.Get("/series", wrapAgent(api.series))
    r.Post("/series", wrapAgent(api.series))
    r.Del("/series", wrapAgent(api.dropSeries))
    // Admin APIs
    r.Post("/admin/tsdb/delete_series", wrapAgent(api.deleteSeries))
}
```

   372→func (api *API) Register(r *route.Router) {
   373→	wrap := func(f apiFunc) http.HandlerFunc {
   374→		hf := http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
   375→			httputil.SetCORS(w, api.CORSOrigin, r)
   376→			result := setUnavailStatusOnTSDBNotReady(f(r))
   377→			if result.finalizer != nil {
   378→				defer result.finalizer()
   379→			}
   380→			if result.err != nil {
   381→				api.respondError(w, result.err, result.data)
   382→				return
   383→			}
   384→
   385→			if result.data != nil {
   386→				api.respond(w, r, result.data, result.warnings, r.FormValue("query"))
   387→				return
   388→			}
   389→			w.WriteHeader(http.StatusNoContent)
   390→		})
   391→		return api.ready(httputil.CompressionHandler{
   392→			Handler: hf,
   393→		}.ServeHTTP)
   394→	}
   395→
   396→	wrapAgent := func(f apiFunc) http.HandlerFunc {
   397→		return wrap(func(r *http.Request) apiFuncResult {
   398→			if api.isAgent {
   399→				return apiFuncResult{nil, &apiError{errorExec, errors.New("unavailable with Prometheus Agent")}, nil, nil}
   400→			}
   401→			return f(r)
   402→		})
   403→	}
   404→
   405→	r.Options("/*path", wrap(api.options))
   406→

   408→	r.Post("/query", wrapAgent(api.query))

  2056→func (api *API) respondError(w http.ResponseWriter, apiErr *apiError, data any) {
  2057→	json := jsoniter.ConfigCompatibleWithStandardLibrary
  2058→	b, err := json.Marshal(&Response{
  2059→		Status:    statusError,
  2060→		ErrorType: apiErr.typ.str,
  2061→		Error:     apiErr.err.Error(),
  2062→		Data:      data,
  2063→	})
  2064→	if err != nil {
  2065→		api.logger.Error("error marshaling json response", "err", err)
  2066→		http.Error(w, err.Error(), http.StatusInternalServerError)
  2067→		return
  2068→	}
  2069→
  2070→	var code int
  2071→	if api.overrideErrorCode != nil {
  2072→		if newCode, override := api.overrideErrorCode(apiErr.typ.num, apiErr.err); override {
  2073→			code = newCode
  2074→		} else {
  2075→			code = getDefaultErrorCode(apiErr.typ)
  2076→		}
  2077→	} else {
  2078→		code = getDefaultErrorCode(apiErr.typ)
  2079→	}
  2080→
  2081→	w.Header().Set("Content-Type", "application/json")
  2082→	w.WriteHeader(code)
  2083→	if n, err := w.Write(b); err != nil {
  2084→		api.logger.Error("error writing response", "bytesWritten", n, "err", err)
  2085→	}
  2086→}
  2087→
  2088→func getDefaultErrorCode(errType errorType) int {
  2089→	switch errType {
  2090→	case errorBadData:
  2091→		return http.StatusBadRequest
  2092→	case errorExec:
  2093→		return http.StatusUnprocessableEntity
  2094→	case errorCanceled:
  2095→		return statusClientClosedConnection
  2096→	case errorTimeout:
  2097→		return http.StatusServiceUnavailable
  2098→	case errorInternal:
  2099→		return http.StatusInternalServerError
  2100→	case errorNotFound:
  2101→		return http.StatusNotFound
  2102→	case errorNotAcceptable:
  2103→		return http.StatusNotAcceptable
  2104→	default:
  2105→		return http.StatusInternalServerError

229-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully implemented the bulk silence creation API for Prometheus. Here's a summary of what was created:

## Implementation Summary

### Files Created/Modified

1. **`web/api/v1/silences_bulk.go`** - New file with the bulk silence endpoint handler
   - Defines the request/response structures:
     - `SilenceMatcher` - Matcher object for silence rules
     - `SilenceRequest` - Single silence creation request
     - `BulkSilenceRequest` - Array of silence creation requests
     - `BulkSilenceResponse` - Response with array of created silence IDs
     - `BulkSilenceError` - Error response with index information
   
   - Implements `silencesBulk()` handler that:
     - Parses JSON request body
     - Validates empty array check
     - Validates all silences before creating any (atomic semantics)
     - Returns array of IDs on success or detailed error with failing index
   
   - Includes validation for:
     - Non-empty matchers list
     - Valid matcher names
     - Valid time ranges (endsAt > startsAt)
     - Required `createdBy` field

2. **`web/api/v1/silences_bulk_test.go`** - New test file with comprehensive test coverage
   - `TestBulkSilenceCreation()` - Tests for the main handler:
     - Successful bulk creation with multiple silences
     - Validation failure on empty matchers
     - Validation failure on invalid matcher (empty name)
     - Empty array handling
     - Partial validation failure (error at specific index)
     - Missing `createdBy` field validation
     - Invalid time range validation
     - Invalid JSON body handling
   
   - `TestBulkSilenceIntegration()` - Integration test with HTTP handler

3. **`web/api/v1/api.go`** - Modified to register the new endpoint
   - Added route: `r.Post("/silences/bulk", wrap(api.silencesBulk))`

// Additionally, if there is no port in the host passed as input, we return the\n1076: // original host, making sure that IPv6 addresses are not surrounded by square\n1077: // brackets.\n1078: func sanitizeSplitHostPort(input string) (string, string, error) {\n1079: \thost, port, err := net.SplitHostPort(input)\n1080: \tif err != nil && strings.HasSuffix(err.Error(), \"missing port in address\") nil {\n1093: \t\treturn u, err\n1094: \t}\n1095: \n1096: \tfor _, lhr := range LocalhostRepresentations {\n1097: \t\tif host == lhr {\n1098: \t\t\t_, ownPort, err := the\n1107: \t\t\t\t// scheme, hostname, and port to the externally reachable ones as\n1108: \t\t\t\t// well. "{\"content\":\"1: ---\\n2: title: HTTP API\\n3: sort_rank: 7\\n4: ---\\n5: \\n6: The current stable HTTP API is reachable under `/api/v1` on a Prometheus\\n7: server. Any non-breaking additions will be added under that endpoint.\\n8: \\n9: ## Format overview\\n10: \\n11: The API response format is JSON. Every successful API request returns a `2xx`\\n12: status code.\\n13: \\n14: Invalid requests that reach the API handlers return a JSON error object\\n15: and one of the following HTTP response codes:\\n16: \\n17: - `400 Bad Request` when parameters are missing or incorrect.\\n18: - `422 Unprocessable Entity` when an expression can't be executed\\n19:   ([RFC4918](https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc4918#page-78)).\\n20: - `503 Service Unavailable` when queries time out or abort.\\n21: \\n22: Other non-`2xx` codes may be returned for errors occurring before the API\\n23: endpoint is reached.\\n24: \\n25: An array of warnings may be returned if there are errors that do\\n26: not inhibit the request execution. An additional array of info-level\\n27: annotations may be returned for potential query issues that may or may\\n28: not be false positives. All of the data that was successfully collected\\n29: will be returned in the data field.\\n30: \\n31: The JSON response envelope format is as follows:\\n32: \\n33: ```json\\n34: {\\n35:   \\\"status\\\": \\\"success\\\" | \\\"error\\\",\\n36:   \\\"data\\\": <data>,\\n37: \\n38:   // Only set if status is \\\"error\\\". The data field may still hold\\n39:   // additional data.\\n40:   \\\"errorType\\\": \\\"<string>\\\",\\n41:   \\\"error\\\": \\\"<string>\\\",\\n42: \\n43:   // Only set if there were warnings while executing the request.\\n44:   // There will still be data in the data field.\\n45:   \\\"warnings\\\": [\\\"<string>\\\"],\\n46:   // Only set if there were info-level annotations while executing the request.\\n47:   \\\"infos\\\": [\\\"<string>\\\"]\\n48: }\\n49: ```\\n50: \\n51: Generic placeholders are defined as follows:\\n52: \\n53: * `<rfc3339 | unix_timestamp>`: Input timestamps may be provided either in\\n54: [RFC3339](https://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc3339.txt) format or as a Unix timestamp\\n55: in seconds, with optional decimal places for sub-second precision. Output\\n56: timestamps are always represented as Unix timestamps in seconds.\\n57: * `<series_selector>`: Prometheus [time series\\n58: selectors](basics.md#time-series-selectors) like `http_requests_total` or\\n59: `http_requests_total{method=~\\\"(GET|POST)\\\"}` and need to be URL-encoded.\\n60: * `<duration>`: [the subset of Prometheus float literals using time units](basics.md#float-literals-and-time-durations).\\n61: For example, `5m` refers to a duration of 5 minutes.\\n62: * `<bool>`: boolean values (strings `true` and `false`).\\n63: \\n64: Note: Names of query parameters that may be repeated end with `[]`.\\n65: \\n66: ## Expression queries\\n67: \\n68: Query language expressions may be evaluated at a single instant or over a range\\n69: of time. The sections below describe the API endpoints for each type of\\n70: expression query.\\n71: \\n72: ### Instant queries\\n73: \\n74: The following endpoint evaluates an instant query at a single point in time:\\n75: \\n76: ```\\n77: GET /api/v1/query\\n78: POST /api/v1/query\\n79: ```\\n80: \\n81: URL query parameters:\\n82: \\n83: - `query=<string>`: Prometheus expression query string.\\n84: - `time=<rfc3339 | unix_timestamp>`: Evaluation timestamp. Optional.\\n85: - `timeout=<duration>`: Evaluation timeout. Optional. Defaults to and\\n86:    is capped by the value of the `-query.timeout` flag.\\n87: - `limit=<number>`: Maximum number of returned series. Doesn\u2019t affect scalars or strings but truncates the number of series for matrices and vectors. Optional. 0 means disabled.\\n88: \\n89: The current server time is used if the `time` parameter is omitted.\\n90: \\n91: You can URL-encode these parameters directly in the request body by using the `POST` method and\\n92: `Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded` header. This is useful when specifying a large\\n93: query that may breach server-side URL character limits.\\n94: \\n95: The `data` section of the query result has the following format:\\n96: \\n97: ```json\\n98: {\\n99:   \\\"resultType\\\": \\\"matrix\\\" | \\\"vector\\\" | \\\"scalar\\\" | \\\"string\\\",\\n100:   \\\"result\\\": <value>\\n101: }\\n102: ```\\n103: \\n104: `<value>` refers to the query result data, which has varying formats\\n105: depending on the `resultType`. See the [expression query result\\n106: formats](#expression-query-result-formats).\\n107: \\n108: The following example evaluates the expression `up` at the time\\n109: `2015-07-01T20:10:51.781Z`:\\n110: \\n111: ```bash\\n112: curl 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=up&time=2015-07-01T20:10:51.781Z'\\n113: ```\\n114: \\n115: ```json\\n116: {\\n117:    \\\"status\\\" : \\\"success\\\",\\n118:    \\\"data\\\" : {\\n119:       \\\"resultType\\\" : \\\"vector\\\",\\n120:       \\\"result\\\" : [\\n121:          {\\n122:             \\\"metric\\\" : {\\n123:                \\\"__name__\\\" : \\\"up\\\",\\n124:                \\\"job\\\" : \\\"prometheus\\\",\\n125:                \\\"instance\\\" : \\\"localhost:9090\\\"\\n126:             },\\n127:             \\\"value\\\": [ 1435781451.781, \\\"1\\\" ]\\n128:          },\\n129:          {\\n130:             \\\"metric\\\" : {\\n131:                \\\"__name__\\\" : \\\"up\\\",\\n132:                \\\"job\\\" : \\\"node\\\",\\n133:                \\\"instance\\\" : \\\"localhost:9100\\\"\\n134:             },\\n135:             \\\"value\\\" : [ 1435781451.781, \\\"0\\\" ]\\n136:          }\\n137:       ]\\n138:    }\\n139: }\\n140: ```\\n141: \\n142: ### Range queries\\n143: \\n144: The following endpoint evaluates an expression query over a range of time:\\n145: \\n146: ```\\n147: GET /api/v1/query_range\\n148: POST /api/v1/query_range\\n149: ```\\n150: \\n151: URL query parameters:\\n152: \\n153: - `query=<string>`: Prometheus expression query string.\\n154: - `start=<rfc3339 | unix_timestamp>`: Start timestamp, inclusive.\\n155: - `end=<rfc3339 | unix_timestamp>`: End timestamp, inclusive.\\n156: - `step=<duration | float>`: Query resolution step width in `duration` format or float number of seconds.\\n157: - `timeout=<duration>`: Evaluation timeout. Optional. Defaults to and\\n158:    is capped by the value of the `-query.timeout` flag.\\n159: - `limit=<number>`: Maximum number of returned series. Optional. 0 means disabled.\\n160: \\n161: You can URL-encode these parameters directly in the request body by using the `POST` method and\\n162: `Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded` header. This is useful when specifying a large\\n163: query that may breach server-side URL character limits.\\n164: \\n165: The `data` section of the query result has the following format:\\n166: \\n167: ```json\\n168: {\\n169:   \\\"resultType\\\": \\\"matrix\\\",\\n170:   \\\"result\\\": <value>\\n171: }\\n172: ```\\n173: \\n174: For the format of the `<value>` placeholder, see the [range-vector result\\n175: format](#range-vectors).\\n176: \\n177: The following example evaluates the expression `up` over a 30-second range with\\n178: a query resolution of 15 seconds.\\n179: \\n180: ```bash\\n181: curl 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query_range?query=up&start=2015-07-01T20:10:30.781Z&end=2015-07-01T20:11:00.781Z&step=15s'\\n182: ```\\n183: \\n184: ```json\\n185: {\\n186:    \\\"status\\\" : \\\"success\\\",\\n187:    \\\"data\\\" : {\\n188:       \\\"resultType\\\" : \\\"matrix\\\",\\n189:       \\\"result\\\" : [\\n190:          {\\n191:             \\\"metric\\\" : {\\n192:                \\\"__name__\\\" : \\\"up\\\",\\n193:                \\\"job\\\" : \\\"prometheus\\\",\\n194:                \\\"instance\\\" : \\\"localhost:9090\\\"\\n195:             },\\n196:             \\\"values\\\" : [\\n197:                [ 1435781430.781, \\\"1\\\" ],\\n198:                [ 1435781445.781, \\\"1\\\" ],\\n199:                [ 1435781460.781, \\\"1\\\" ]\\n200:             ]\\n201:          },\\n202:          {\\n203:             \\\"metric\\\" : {\\n204:                \\\"__name__\\\" : \\\"up\\\",\\n205:                \\\"job\\\" : \\\"node\\\",\\n206:                \\\"instance\\\" : \\\"localhost:9091\\\"\\n207:             },\\n208:             \\\"values\\\" : [\\n209:                [ 1435781430.781, \\\"0\\\" ],\\n210:                [ 1435781445.781, \\\"0\\\" ],\\n211:                [ 1435781460.781, \\\"1\\\" ]\\n212:             ]\\n213:          }\\n214:       ]\\n215:    }\\n216: }\\n217: ```\\n218: \\n219: ## Formatting query expressions\\n220: \\n221: The following endpoint formats a PromQL expression in a prettified way:\\n222: \\n223: ```\\n224: GET /api/v1/format_query\\n225: POST /api/v1/format_query\\n226: ```\\n227: \\n228: URL query parameters:\\n229: \\n230: - `query=<string>`: Prometheus expression query string.\\n231: \\n232: You can URL-encode these parameters directly in the request body by using the `POST` method and\\n233: `Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded` header. This is useful when specifying a large\\n234: query that may breach server-side URL character limits.\\n235: \\n236: The `data` section of the query result is a string containing the formatted query expression. Note that any comments are removed in the formatted string.\\n237: \\n238: The following example formats the expression `foo/bar`:\\n239: \\n240: ```bash\\n241: curl 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/format_query?query=foo/bar'\\n242: ```\\n243: \\n244: ```json\\n245: {\\n246:    \\\"status\\\" : \\\"success\\\",\\n247:    \\\"data\\\" : \\\"foo / bar\\\"\\n248: }\\n249: ```\\n250: \\n251: ## Parsing a PromQL expressions into a abstract syntax tree (AST)\\n252: \\n253: This endpoint is **experimental** and might change in the future. It is currently only meant to be used by Prometheus' own web UI, and the endpoint name and exact format returned may change from one Prometheus version to another. It may also be removed again in case it is no longer needed by the UI.\\n254: \\n255: The following endpoint parses a PromQL expression and returns it as a JSON-formatted AST (abstract syntax tree) representation:\\n256: \\n257: ```\\n258: GET /api/v1/parse_query\\n259: POST /api/v1/parse_query\\n260: ```\\n261: \\n262: URL query parameters:\\n263: \\n264: - `query=<string>`: Prometheus expression query string.\\n265: \\n266: You can URL-encode these parameters directly in the request body by using the `POST` method and\\n267: `Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded` header. This is useful when specifying a large\\n268: query that may breach server-side URL character limits.\\n269: \\n270: The `data` section of the query result is a string containing the AST of the parsed query expression.\\n271: \\n272: The following example parses the expression `foo/bar`:\\n273: \\n274: ```bash\\n275: curl 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/parse_query?query=foo/bar'\\n276: ```\\n277: \\n278: ```json\\n279: {\\n280:    \\\"data\\\" : {\\n281:       \\\"bool\\\" : false,\\n282:       \\\"lhs\\\" : {\\n283:          \\\"matchers\\\" : [\\n284:             {\\n285:                \\\"name\\\" : \\\"__name__\\\",\\n286:                \\\"type\\\" : \\\"=\\\",\\n287:                \\\"value\\\" : \\\"foo\\\"\\n288:             }\\n289:          ],\\n290:          \\\"name\\\" : \\\"foo\\\",\\n291:          \\\"offset\\\" : 0,\\n292:          \\\"startOrEnd\\\" : null,\\n293:          \\\"timestamp\\\" : null,\\n294:          \\\"type\\\" : \\\"vectorSelector\\\"\\n295:       },\\n296:       \\\"matching\\\" : {\\n297:          \\\"card\\\" : \\\"one-to-one\\\",\\n298:          \\\"include\\\" : [],\\n299:          \\\"labels\\\" : [],\\n300:          \\\"on\\\" : false\\n301: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4@ba16cf5a7437eb3b6b71b74557b7a67e1975ad0f/-/blob/docs/querying/api.md%3FL1-300\"}"

`json:\"droppedTargetCounts\"`\n}\n\n// GlobalURLOptions contains fields used for deriving the global URL for local targets.\ntype GlobalURLOptions struct {\n\tListenAddress string\n\tHost          string\n\tScheme        string\n}\n\n// sanitizeSplitHostPort acts like net.SplitHostPort.\n// Additionally, if there is no port in the host passed as input, we return the\n// original host, making sure that IPv6 addresses are not surrounded by square\n// brackets.\nfunc sanitizeSplitHostPort(input string) (string, string, error) {\n\thost, port, err := net.SplitHostPort(input)\n\tif err != nil && strings.HasSuffix(err.Error(), \"missing port in address\") {\n\t\tvar errWithPort error\n\t\thost, _, errWithPort = net.SplitHostPort(input + \":80\")\n\t\tif errWithPort == nil {\n\t\t\terr = nil\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn host, port, err\n}\n\nfunc getGlobalURL(u *url.URL, opts GlobalURLOptions) (*url.URL, error) {\n\thost, port, err := sanitizeSplitHostPort(u.Host)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn u, err\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, lhr := range LocalhostRepresentations {\n\t\tif host == lhr {\n\t\t\t_, ownPort, err := net.SplitHostPort(opts.ListenAddress)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn u, err\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tif port == ownPort {\n\t\t\t\t// Only in the case where the target is on localhost and its port is\n\t\t\t\t// the same as the one we're listening on, we know for sure that\n\t\t\t\t// we're monitoring our own process and that we need to change the\n\t\t\t\t// scheme, hostname, and port to the externally reachable ones as\n\t\t\t\t// well. We shouldn't need to touch the path at all, since if a\n\t\t\t\t// path prefix is defined, the path under which we scrape ourselves\n\t\t\t\t// should already contain the prefix.\n\t\t\t\tu.Scheme = opts.Scheme\n\t\t\t\tu.Host = opts.Host\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// Otherwise, we only know that localhost is not reachable\n\t\t\t\t// externally, so we replace only the hostname by the one in the\n\t\t\t\t// external URL. It could be the wrong hostname for the service on\n\t\t\t\t// this port, but it's still the best possible guess.\n\t\t\t\thost, _, err := sanitizeSplitHostPort(opts.Host)\n\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn u, err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tu.Host = host\n\t\t\t\tif port != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\t\tu.Host = net.JoinHostPort(u.Host, port)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn u, nil\n}\n\nfunc (api *API) scrapePools(r *http.Request) apiFuncResult {\n\tnames := api.scrapePoolsRetriever(r.Context()).ScrapePools()\n\tsort.Strings(names)\n\tres := matchers {\n\t\tif !m.Matches(lset.Get(m.Name)) {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn true\n}\n\nfunc (api *API) targetMetadata(r *http.Request) apiFuncResult {\n\tlimit := -1\n\tif s := map[metadata.Metadata]struct{}{}\n\t\t\t\t\tmetrics[md.MetricFamily] = ms\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tms[m] = struct{}{}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Put the elements from the pseudo-set into a slice for \"pending\", \"firing\", \"inactive\".\n\tState          string           `json:\"state\"`\n\tName           string           `json:\"name\"`\n\tQuery          string \"alerting\".\n\tType string `json:\"type\"`\n}\n\ntype RecordingRule struct {\n\tName           string           `json:\"name\"`\n\tQuery          string           `json:\"query\"`\n\tLabels `json:\"evaluationTime\"`\n\tLastEvaluation time.Time        `json:\"lastEvaluation\"`\n\t// Type of a recordingRule is always \"recording\".\n\tType string `json:\"type\"`\n}\n\nfunc (api *API) rules(r *http.Request) apiFuncResult {\n\tif err := r.ParseForm(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn apiFuncResult{nil, &apiError{errorBadData, fmt.Errorf(\"error parsing form values: %w\", err)}, nil, nil}\n\t}\n\n\tqueryFormToSet := func(values []string) map[string]struct{} {\n\t\tset := make(map[string]struct{}, len(values))\n\t\tfor _, v := range values {\n\t\t\tset[v] = struct{}{}\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn set\n\t}\n\n\trnSet := queryFormToSet(r.Form[\"rule_name[]\"])\n\trgSet := queryFormToSet(r.Form[\"rule_group[]\"])\n\tfSet := queryFormToSet(r.Form[\"file[]\"])\n\n\tmatcherSets, err := parseMatchersParam(r.Form[\"match[]\"])\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn apiFuncResult{nil, &apiError{errorBadData, err}, nil, strings.ToLower(r.URL.Query().Get(\"type\"))\n\n\tif typ != \"\" && typ != \"alert\" && typ != \"record\" {\n\t\treturn invalidParamError(fmt.Errorf(\"not supported value %q\", typ), \"type\")\n\t}\n\n\treturnAlerts := typ == \"\" || typ == \"alert\"\n\treturnRecording := typ == \"\" || typ == \"record\"\n\n\texcludeAlerts, err := parseExcludeAlerts(r)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn invalidParamError(err, \"exclude_alerts\")\n\t}\n\n\tmaxGroups, nextToken, parseErr := parseListRulesPaginationRequest(r)\n\tif parseErr != nil {\n\t\treturn *parseErr\n\t}\n\n\trgs := make([]*RuleGroup, 0, len(ruleGroups))\n\n\tfoundToken := false\n\n\tfor _, grp := range ruleGroups {\n\t\tif maxGroups > 0 && nextToken != \"\" && !foundToken {\n\t\t\tif nextToken != getRuleGroupNextToken(grp.File(), grp.Name()) {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tfoundToken = true\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif len(rgSet) > 0 {\n\t\t\tif _, ok := rgSet[grp.Name()]; !ok {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif len(fSet) > 0 {\n\t\t\tif _, ok := fSet[grp.File()]; !ok {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tapiRuleGroup := &RuleGroup{\n\t\t\tName:           grp.Name(),\n\t\t\tFile:           grp.File(),\n\t\t\tInterval:       grp.Interval().Seconds(),\n\t\t\tLimit:          grp.Limit(),\n\t\t\tRules:          []Rule{},\n\t\t\tEvaluationTime: grp.GetEvaluationTime().Seconds(),\n\t\t\tLastEvaluation: grp.GetLastEvaluation(),\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tfor _, rr := range grp.Rules(matcherSets...) {\n\t\t\tvar enrichedRule Rule\n\n\t\t\tif len(rnSet) > 0 {\n\t\t\t\tif _, ok := rnSet[rr.Name()]; !ok {\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tlastError := \"\"\n\t\t\tif rr.LastError() != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlastError = rr.LastError().Error()\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tswitch rule := rr.(type) {\n\t\t\tcase *rules.AlertingRule:\n\t\t\t\tif !returnAlerts {\n\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tvar activeAlerts []*Alert\n\t\t\t\tif !excludeAlerts {\n\t\t\t\t\tactiveAlerts = rulesAlertsToAPIAlerts(rule.ActiveAlerts())\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t\tenrichedRule = AlertingRule{\n\t\t\t\t\tState:          rule.State().String(),\n\t\t\t\t\tName:           rule.Name(),\n\t\t\t\t\tQuery:          rule.Query().String(),\n\t\t\t\t\tDuration:       rule.HoldDuration().Seconds(),\n\t\t\t\t\tKeepFiringFor:  rule.KeepFiringFor().Seconds(),\n\t\t\t\t\tLabels:         rule.Labels(),\n\t\t\t\t\tAnnotations:    rule.Annotations(),\n\t\t\t\t\tAlerts:         activeAlerts,\n\t\t\t\t\tHealth:         rule.Health(),\n\t\t\t\t\tLastError:      lastError,\n\t\t\t\t\tEvaluationTime: rule.GetEvaluationDuration().Seconds(),\n\t\t\t\t\tLastEvaluation: rule.GetEvaluationTimestamp(),\n\t\t\t\t\tType:           \"alerting\",\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tcase *rules.RecordingRule:\n\t\t\t\tif !returnRecording {\n\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tenrichedRule = RecordingRule{\n\t\t\t\t\tName:           rule.Name(),\n\t\t\t\t\tQuery:          rule.Query().String(),\n\t\t\t\t\tLabels:         rule.Labels(),\n\t\t\t\t\tHealth:         rule.Health(),\n\t\t\t\t\tLastError:      lastError,\n\t\t\t\t\tEvaluationTime: rule.GetEvaluationDuration().Seconds(),\n\t\t\t\t\tLastEvaluation: rule.GetEvaluationTimestamp(),\n\t\t\t\t\tType:           \"recording\",\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\terr := fmt.Errorf(\"failed to assert type of rule '%v'\", rule.Name())\n\t\t\t\treturn apiFuncResult{nil, &apiError{errorInternal, err}, nil, nil}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tif enrichedRule != nil {\n\t\t\t\tapiRuleGroup.Rules = append(apiRuleGroup.Rules, enrichedRule)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// If the rule group response has no rules, skip it - this means we filtered all the rules of this group.\n\t\tif len(apiRuleGroup.Rules) > 0 {\n\t\t\tif maxGroups > 0 && len(rgs) == int(maxGroups) {\n\t\t\t\t// We've reached the capacity of our page plus one. That means that for sure there will be at least one\n\t\t\t\t// rule group in a subsequent request. Therefore a next token is required.\n\t\t\t\tres.GroupNextToken = getRuleGroupNextToken(grp.File(), grp.Name())\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\trgs = append(rgs, apiRuleGroup)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tif maxGroups > 0 && nextToken != \"\" && !foundToken {\n\t\treturn invalidParamError(fmt.Errorf(\"invalid group_next_token '%v'. were rule groups changed?\", nextToken), \"group_next_token\")\n\t}\n\n\tres.RuleGroups = rgs\n\treturn apiFuncResult{res, nil, nil, nil}\n}\n\nfunc parseExcludeAlerts(r *http.Request) (bool, error) {\n\texcludeAlertsParam := strings.ToLower(r.URL.Query().Get(\"exclude_alerts\"))\n\n\tif excludeAlertsParam == \"\" {\n\t\treturn false, nil\n\t}\n\n\texcludeAlerts, err := strconv.ParseBool(excludeAlertsParam)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn false, fmt.Errorf(\"error converting exclude_alerts: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\treturn excludeAlerts, nil\n}\n\nfunc parseListRulesPaginationRequest(r *http.Request) (int64, string, *apiFuncResult) {\n\tvar (\n\t\tparsedMaxGroups int64 = -1\n\t\terr             error\n\t)\n\tmaxGroups := r.URL.Query().Get(\"group_limit\")\n\tnextToken := r.URL.Query().Get(\"group_next_token\")\n\n\tif nextToken != \"\" && maxGroups == \"\" {\n\t\terrResult := invalidParamError(errors.New(\"group_limit needs to be present in order to paginate over the groups\"), \"group_next_token\")\n\t\treturn -1, \"\", &errResult\n\t}\n\n\tif maxGroups != \"\" {\n\t\tparsedMaxGroups, err = strconv.ParseInt(maxGroups, 10, 32)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\terrResult := invalidParamError(fmt.Errorf(\"group_limit needs to be a valid number: %w\", err), \"group_limit\")\n\t\t\treturn -1, \"\", &errResult\n\t\t}\n\t\tif parsedMaxGroups <= 0 {\n\t\t\terrResult := invalidParamError(errors.New(\"group_limit needs to be greater than 0\"), \"group_limit\")\n\t\t\treturn -1, \"\", &errResult\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tif parsedMaxGroups > 0 {\n\t\treturn parsedMaxGroups, nextToken, nil\n\t}\n\n\treturn -1, \"\", nil\n}\n\nfunc getRuleGroupNextToken(file, group string) string {\n\th := sha1.New()\n\th.Write([]byte(file + \";\" + group))\n\treturn hex.EncodeToString(h.Sum(nil))\n}\n\ntype prometheusConfig struct {\n\tYAML string `json:\"yaml\"`\n}\n\nfunc (api *API) serveRuntimeInfo(*http.Request) apiFuncResult {\n\tstatus, err := package v1

import (
	"encoding/json"
	"fmt"
	"net/http"
	"time"
)

// SilenceMatcher represents a matcher for silence rules.
type SilenceMatcher struct {
	Name    string `json:"name"`
	Value   string `json:"value"`
	IsRegex bool   `json:"isRegex"`
}

// SilenceRequest represents a single silence creation request.
type SilenceRequest struct {
	Matchers  []SilenceMatcher `json:"matchers"`
	StartsAt  *time.Time       `json:"startsAt,omitempty"`
	EndsAt    *time.Time       `json:"endsAt,omitempty"`
	CreatedBy string           `json:"createdBy"`
	Comment   string           `json:"comment"`
}

// BulkSilenceRequest represents a bulk silence creation request.
type BulkSilenceRequest struct {
	Silences []SilenceRequest `json:"silences"`
}

// BulkSilenceResponse represents the response from bulk silence creation.
type BulkSilenceResponse struct {
	IDs []string `json:"ids"`
}

// BulkSilenceError represents an error in bulk silence creation with index information.
type BulkSilenceError struct {
	Index   int    `json:"index"`
	Message string `json:"message"`
}

// silencesBulk handles POST requests for creating multiple silences atomically.
func (api *API) silencesBulk(r *http.Request) apiFunc
... (truncated)

func TestBulkSilenceCreation(t *testing.T) {
	// Test successful bulk creation
	t.Run("successful_bulk_creation", func(t *testing.T) {
		api := &API{
			ready: func(f http.HandlerFunc) http.HandlerFunc { return f },
		}

		bulkReq := BulkSilenceRequest{
			Silences: []SilenceRequest{
				{
					Matchers: []SilenceMatcher{
						{Name: "alertname", Value: "TestAlert", IsRegex: false},
					},
					CreatedBy: "test_user",
					Comment:   "Test silence 1",
				},
				{
					Matchers: []SilenceMatcher{
						{Name: "instance", Value: "localhost:9090", IsRegex: false},
					},
					CreatedBy: "test_user",
					Comment:   "Test silence 2",
				},
			},
		}

		body, err := json.Marshal(bulkReq)
		require.NoError(t, err)

		req := httptest.NewRequest("POST", "/api/v1/silences/bulk", bytes.NewReader(body))
		req = req.WithContext(context.Background())

		result := api.silencesBulk(req)
		require.NoError(t, result.err.err)
		require.NotNil(t, result.data)

		resp, ok := result.data.(BulkSilenceResponse)
		require.True(t, ok)
		require.Le

Features:
